<div id='chapter-1'></div>

# Chapter 1: The Perfection of Generosity (Dānapāramitā)

---

## Invocation and Opening Kārikās (Root Verses 1-8)

### Kārikā 1: The Call to Listen

> **yasyāśraveṇa narakādimahāpratāpa-**
> **dāhādiduḥkhamanubhūtamabhūdbhavadbhiḥ |**
> **tīvraṃ punaḥ punaranantamaśāntacittai-**
> **stacchrotumādaramudārataraṃ bhajadhvam ||1||**

*That [teaching],¹ through the hearing of which² the intense, repeated, endless suffering—the great burning³ and other torments of hell and other [realms]—experienced by you whose minds are unquiet, ceases to exist:⁴ cultivate with most excellent respect [the desire] to hear that!*⁵

---

### Kārikā 2: The Power of Hearing

> **śrutvā [ca yaṃ tyajati] pāpamanuddhatātmā**
> **pūrvārjitaṃ ca vipulaṃ kṣapayatyaśeṣam |**
> **aprāptapūrvamapi saukhyamavāpnuvanti**
> **hāniṃsukhācca na kadācidapi prayānti ||2||**

*Having heard [this teaching], one whose mind is not arrogant³ abandons evil and exhausts completely the vast [karmic debt] accumulated in the past. Such persons attain happiness never before obtained, and never again do they fall from that bliss.*

---

### Kārikā 3: The Rare Treasure

> **saṃbodhisattvasukhamuttamamakṣayaṃ [ca]**
> **[...]pyasamasaṃpadamāpnuvanti |**
> **taddharmaratnamatidurlabhamadya labdhaṃ**
> **labdhakṣaṇāḥ śṛṇuta sādaramucyamānam ||3||**

*[They] attain the supreme, inexhaustible happiness of perfect awakening⁴ and unequalled spiritual wealth. That jewel of Dharma, so exceedingly rare to obtain, has been obtained today. You who have gained this [precious] opportunity⁵—listen respectfully as it is proclaimed!*

---

### Kārikā 4: Invitation to All Beings

> **āyāntu ca tribhuvanaikahitasya vākyaṃ**
> **śrotuṃ prasannamanasaḥ suranāgasattvāḥ |**
> **gandharvayakṣagaruḍāsurakinnarendrāḥ**
> **pretādayaḥ śravaṇajātatṛṣaḥ saharṣāḥ ||4||**

*Let gods, nāgas,⁶ and [all] beings come with serene minds to hear the words of the One whose sole purpose is the benefit of the three worlds.⁷ Let gandharvas, yakṣas, garuḍas, asuras, kinnara lords, hungry ghosts, and others come with joy, thirsting to hear!*

---

### Kārikā 5: The Author's Purpose

> **sugatān sasutān sadharmakāyān**
> **praṇipatyādarato'khilāṃśca vandyān |**
> **sugatātmajasaṃvarāvatāraṃ**
> **kathayiṣyāmi samuccitārthavākyaiḥ ||5||**

*Having bowed with reverence to the Sugatas⁸ together with their sons⁹ and [their] Dharma-bodies,¹⁰ and to all who are worthy of worship, I shall expound the entrance into the discipline of the Sugata's offspring¹¹ with carefully compiled meaningful statements.*

---

### Kārikā 6: Humility

> **na ca kiṃcidapūrvamatra vācyaṃ**
> **na ca saṃgrathanakauśalaṃ mamāsti |**
> **ata eva na me parārthayatnaḥ**
> **svamano bhāvayituṃ mamedamiṣṭam ||6||**

*Nothing new is to be said here, nor do I possess skill in composition.¹² Therefore this effort is not for the benefit of others—my wish is simply to cultivate my own mind.*¹³

---

### Kārikā 7: Potential Benefit

> **mama tāvadanena yāti vṛddhiṃ**
> **kuśalaṃ bhāvayituṃ prasādavegaḥ |**
> **yadi matsamadhātureva paśyed**
> **aparo'pyenamato'pi sārthako'yam ||7||**

*Through this [work], my impetus of faith¹⁴ for cultivating virtue increases. If another of similar disposition should see [this compilation], then from that [perspective] too, this is meaningful.*

---

### Kārikā 8: The Precious Opportunity

> **kṣaṇasaṃpadiyaṃ sudurlabhā**
> **pratilabdhā puruṣārthasādhanī |**
> **yadi nātra vicintyate hitaṃ**
> **punarapyeṣa samāgamaḥ kutaḥ ||8||**

*This endowment of favorable circumstances¹⁵ is extremely difficult to obtain, [yet] it has been obtained—it accomplishes the goal of human life. If one does not reflect upon what is beneficial here [and now], from where will such an opportunity come again?*

---

## The Rarity of Human Birth: Quotation from Gaṇḍavyūhasūtra

As stated in the Āryagaṇḍavyūhasūtra,¹⁶ in the Liberation [chapter on] Āryajayoṣmāyatana:¹⁷

> *"Rare is the cessation of the eight unfavorable conditions.¹⁸ Rare is obtaining a human body. Rare is the purity of favorable circumstances. Rare is the arising of a Buddha. Rare is the possession of complete sense faculties. Rare is hearing the Buddha-dharma. Rare is association with good persons.*
> 
> *Rare are genuine spiritual friends. Rare is proper instruction in the true method. Rare is right livelihood. Rare is compatible effort in the true Dharma in the human world."*

---

## Footnotes

¹ **[Sanskrit]** *yasya*: Relative pronoun genitive, "that [teaching] of which..." The relative-correlative structure (*yasya...tat*) is characteristic of Sanskrit philosophical verse.

² **[Sanskrit]** *āśraveṇa*: Instrumental of *āśrava* (hearing). "Through the hearing of which"—the teaching is efficacious *through being heard*.

³ **[Sanskrit]** *mahāpratāpa-dāha*: "Great fierceness-burning"—the intense heat of hell realms.

⁴ **[Sanskrit]** *abhūt*: "Becomes non-existent" (√bhū with negation via sandhi). The suffering *ceases* through hearing the teaching.

⁵ **[Meter]** This and the following verses are in *śārdūlavikrīḍita* meter (19 syllables per quarter), more elaborate than the *anuṣṭubh* typical of Buddhist śāstras. **[Grammar]** *bhajadhvam* is 2nd person plural imperative—a direct command to the assembly.

³ **[Sanskrit]** *anuddhatātmā*: "one whose self is not arrogant/agitated." Compound of *an-uddhata* + *ātman*.

⁴ **[Sanskrit]** *saṃbodhisattvasukham*: The happiness of perfect awakening. *Saṃbodhi* = complete enlightenment.

⁵ **[Sanskrit]** *labdhakṣaṇāḥ*: "having obtained the [opportune] moment." *Kṣaṇa* here refers to the precious human rebirth with all its conditions.

⁶ **[Sanskrit]** *nāga*: Serpent-beings of the underworld/water realm, often protectors of Dharma.

⁷ **[Sanskrit]** *tribhuvana*: The three worlds—desire realm, form realm, formless realm; or alternatively earth, heaven, and the underworld.

⁸ **[Sanskrit]** *sugata*: "Well-Gone One," an epithet of Buddha. From *su-* (well) + *gata* (gone).

⁹ **[Sanskrit]** *sasutān*: "together with [their] sons." The *suta*/*putra* (children/sons) are the bodhisattvas.

¹⁰ **[Sanskrit]** *dharmakāya*: The "Dharma-body," the ultimate truth-body of Buddha, identical with reality itself.

¹¹ **[Sanskrit]** *sugatātmajasaṃvara*: The discipline (*saṃvara*) of the offspring (*ātmaja*) of the Sugata—i.e., bodhisattva vows.

¹² **[Cross-ref]** This verse parallels Bodhicaryāvatāra 1.2 almost exactly, showing the texts' close relationship.

¹³ **[Philosophical]** Śāntideva's characteristic humility—he claims no originality but presents the teaching for his own practice.

¹⁴ **[Sanskrit]** *prasādavega*: "impetus/momentum of faith." *Prasāda* = clarity, serenity, faith.

¹⁵ **[Sanskrit]** *kṣaṇasaṃpad*: "endowment of the [opportune] moment"—the 18 conditions for a precious human rebirth.

¹⁶ **[Source]** *Āryagaṇḍavyūhasūtra*: The "Flower Ornament Sūtra" (Avataṃsaka), one of the most extensive Mahāyāna sūtras.

¹⁷ **[Source]** The *Jayoṣmāyatanavimokṣa* is a liberation chapter within the Gaṇḍavyūha describing the spiritual attainments of a teacher named Jayoṣmāyatana.

¹⁸ **[Philosophical]** *aṣṭākṣaṇa*: The eight unfavorable conditions that prevent Dharma practice: (1) hell, (2) hungry ghost realm, (3) animal realm, (4) long-lived gods, (5) barbarian lands, (6) wrong views, (7) Buddha-less eon, (8) defective sense faculties.

---

## Key Concepts

- **Kṣaṇasaṃpad** (क्षणसम्पद्): The "endowment of the opportune moment"—the 18 favorable conditions for Dharma practice
- **Sugatātmajasaṃvara** (सुगतात्मजसंवर): The discipline/vows of the Sugata's offspring—bodhisattva precepts
- **Aṣṭākṣaṇa** (अष्टाक्षण): The eight unfavorable conditions that obstruct practice

---

## Soul-Check Hints for Blues Version

- The opening is an *invitation*—call-and-response energy
- Verse 6's humility: "I ain't saying nothing new, just trying to fix my own heart"
- Verse 8's urgency: "This chance don't come twice"
- The Gaṇḍavyūha quotation is a *litany of rarities*—could be treated as congregational testimony


### Part 2: Faith as Foundation and the Arising of Bodhicitta


## The Arising of Bodhicitta in the Great Being

Having encountered such an opportunity, one who has well understood the suffering of saṃsāra from both conventional and ultimate perspectives, and who aspires to the peace of its cessation—through the influence of the Buddha-gotra,¹ this reflection arises in such a great being:

### Verse from [Bodhicaryāvatāra 1.1]²

> **yadā mama pareṣāṃ ca bhayaṃ duḥkhaṃ ca na priyam |**
> **tadātmanaḥ ko viśeṣo yattaṃ rakṣāmi netaram ||**

*When neither fear nor suffering is dear to me or to others, what distinction is there in the self such that I protect it and not the other?*

Thus, for the sake of oneself and the realm of beings:

### Kārikā [2]³

> **duḥkhāntaṃ kartukāmena sukhāntaṃ gantumicchatā |**
> **śraddhāmūlaṃ dṛḍhīkṛtya bodhau kāryā matirdṛḍhā ||**

*By one who wishes to make an end of suffering, by one who desires to reach the culmination of happiness: having made firm the root of faith, a firm resolve toward awakening must be made.*


## The Glory of Faith: Quotation from Ratnolkā-dhāraṇī

As stated in the Ratnolkā-dhāraṇī:⁴

> *By faith one follows the Victors;⁵ by faith one trusts the Victor's Dharma; by faith in the conduct of the Buddha's sons⁶ arises the mind of great beings toward unsurpassed awakening.*
>
> *Faith goes before, like a mother, like a guide; it protects and increases all good qualities. It dispels doubt, ferries one across the flood,⁷ it shows the way, is the forerunner of patience.*
>
> *Faith is the clarity of an undefiled mind; it is the root of respect, free from pride. Faith is the treasure-store of wealth, the chief of good conduct—like a hand, it is the root of gathering virtue.*
>
> *Faith produces joy in giving; faith produces delight in the Buddha-dharma. Faith creates distinction in the knowledge of qualities; it leads one to the Buddha-path.*
>
> *For sharpness and radiance of the faculties—faith is the power. For invincibility—faith. For being unassailable by afflictions—faith in the qualities of the Self-Arisen Ones.*
>
> *Faith is non-attachment to the pleasures of attachment; it avoids unfavorable moments, foremost in [seizing] the opportune moment. Faith crosses beyond the path of Māra;⁸ it shows the supreme path of liberation.*
>
> *Faith is the uncorrupted seed, the cause of qualities; faith makes the bodhi-tree⁹ sprout. It increases wisdom, distinction, and happiness; faith reveals all the Victors.*
>
> *Those who ever have faith and respect for the Buddha—they do not abandon discipline or training. Those who do not abandon discipline or training—they are praised as virtuous, those who possess virtue.*
>
> *Those who ever have faith and respect for the Dharma—they listen insatiably to the Victor's Dharma. Those who listen insatiably to the Victor's Dharma—in them arises conviction in the inconceivable Dharma.*
>
> *Those who ever have faith and respect for the Saṅgha—they are irreversible, devoted to the Saṅgha. Those irreversible, devoted to the Saṅgha—they are irreversible through the power of faith.*
>
> *Those irreversible through the power of faith—their faculties are sharp and radiant. Those whose faculties are sharp and radiant—they have abandoned evil companions.*
>
> *Those who have abandoned evil companions—they embrace dharmic friends.¹⁰ Those who embrace dharmic friends—they accumulate vast merit.*
>
> *Those who accumulate vast merit—they are great beings endowed with the power of causes. Great beings endowed with the power of causes—they have distinguished noble conviction.*
>
> *Those with distinguished noble conviction—they are ever blessed by all the Victors. Those ever blessed by all the Victors—in them arises the mind of awakening.*
>
> *Those in whom arises the mind of awakening—they are devoted to the qualities of the great ṛṣis. Those devoted to the qualities of the great ṛṣis—they are born in the Buddha-family, well-born.*
>
> *Those born in the Buddha-family, well-born—they are freed from [wrong] connection and disconnection. Those freed from connection and disconnection—their disposition is purified with clarity.*
>
> *Those whose disposition is purified with clarity—their higher disposition is supreme and excellent. Those whose higher disposition is supreme—they ever practice the perfections.*
>
> *Those who ever practice the perfections—they have entered the Great Vehicle here. Those who have entered the Great Vehicle—they worship the Buddhas through practice.*
>
> *Those who worship the Buddhas through practice—in them recollection of Buddha is undefiled. Those in whom recollection of Buddha is undefiled—they ever see and contemplate the Buddhas.*
>
> *Those who ever see and contemplate the Buddhas—the Buddha never stands apart from them. Those from whom the Buddha never stands apart—the Dharma never departs from them.*
>
> *Those from whom the Dharma never departs—they are ever blessed by all the Victors.*

Thus is the endless elaboration of the root of faith spoken there. Having completed that [section], it concludes briefly:

> *Rare among ordinary sentient beings are those who have faith in such Dharmas. But those who have accumulated virtue and made merit—they have faith through the power of causes.*
>
> *One who might attend upon beings equal to the dust of ten fields¹¹ for a kalpa with all happiness—that merit is not as great as the merit of one who has faith in these Dharmas.*


## Additional Testimonies on Faith

### From Āryadadaśadharmasūtra¹²

> *Faith is the supreme vehicle by which the guides depart. Therefore the wise person should cultivate following faith.*
>
> *For one without faith, white dharmas do not grow—like green shoots from seeds burned by fire.*

### From Āryalalitavistarasūtra¹³

*"Ānanda, effort should be made in faith. This the Tathāgata declares."*

### From Siṃhaparipṛcchā¹⁴

*"Through faith, one avoids unfavorable moments."*


## Making Bodhicitta Firm

Thus, having made firm the root of faith, bodhicitta must be made firm, since it encompasses all merit. As stated in the Āryasiṃhaparipṛcchā, when the Blessed One was questioned by Prince Siṃha:

> **saṃgrahaḥ sarvadharmāṇāṃ karmaṇā kena jāyate |**
> **priyaśca bhoti sattvānāṃ yatra yatropapadyate ||**

*"By what action does the encompassing of all dharmas arise? And [how does one become] dear to beings wherever one is reborn?"*

The Blessed One said:

> **sarvasattvapramokṣāya cittaṃ bodhāya nāmayet |**
> **eṣa saṃgraha dharmāṇāṃ bhavate tena ca priyaḥ ||**

*"One should bend the mind toward awakening for the liberation of all beings. This is the encompassing of dharmas; thereby one becomes dear [to all]."*


## The Glories of Bodhicitta: Quotation from Gaṇḍavyūhasūtra

Likewise in the Āryagaṇḍavyūhasūtra it is described:

> *"Bodhicitta, son of good family, is the seed of all Buddha-dharmas. It is the field for the growth of white dharmas of all the world.¹⁵ It is the ground as refuge for all the world... It is like a father for the protection of all bodhisattvas.*
>
> *...It is like Vaiśravaṇa¹⁶ for cutting off all poverty. It is like the wish-fulfilling gem-king for accomplishing all purposes. It is like the auspicious pot¹⁷ for fulfilling all intentions. It is like a spear for conquering the enemy of afflictions. It is like Dharma for cutting off improper mental engagement.*
>
> *It is like a sword for severing the head of afflictions. It is like an axe for cutting the tree of suffering. It is like a weapon for protecting from all dangers. It is like a hook for drawing beings out of the waters of saṃsāra. It is like a whirlwind for scattering the grass of all obscurations and hindrances.*
>
> *It is like a summary for collecting all the vows and aspirations of bodhisattvas. It is like a caitya for the world with its gods, humans, and asuras.*
>
> *Thus, son of good family, bodhicitta is endowed with these and other immeasurable distinct qualities."*


## Footnotes

¹ **[Sanskrit]** *buddhagotra*: The "Buddha-lineage" or "Buddha-nature"—the innate capacity for awakening present in all beings.

² **[Cross-ref]** This verse is from Bodhicaryāvatāra 8.120, here cited to establish the foundation of equal concern for self and other.

³ **[Kārikā]** This is root verse 2 of the Śikṣāsamuccayakārikā, Śāntideva's own mnemonic summary.

⁴ **[Source]** *Ratnolkā-dhāraṇī*: The "Torch of Jewels Dhāraṇī," an early Mahāyāna scripture emphasizing faith (śraddhā).

⁵ **[Sanskrit]** *jina*: "Victor," an epithet for Buddha.

⁶ **[Sanskrit]** *buddhasutānām*: "of the Buddha's sons"—the bodhisattvas.

⁷ **[Sanskrit]** *ogha*: "flood"—the flood of saṃsāra, the four floods (desire, existence, views, ignorance).

⁸ **[Sanskrit]** *mārapatha*: The path of Māra, the tempter/obstructor; the way of spiritual danger.

⁹ **[Sanskrit]** *bodhidruma*: The "awakening tree"—the tree under which Buddha attained enlightenment; metaphorically, the "tree" of awakening itself.

¹⁰ **[Sanskrit]** *dhārmikamitra*: "Dharmic friends"—spiritual friends who support one's practice. Also called *kalyāṇamitra*.

¹¹ **[Sanskrit]** *daśakṣetrarajopamasatvān*: Beings equal in number to the dust particles of ten buddha-fields—an inconceivably vast number.

¹² **[Source]** *Āryadadaśadharmasūtra*: The "Holy Sūtra of Ten Dharmas."

¹³ **[Source]** *Lalitavistarasūtra*: The extended life story of the Buddha.

¹⁴ **[Source]** *Siṃhaparipṛcchā*: "Questions of [Prince] Lion."

¹⁵ **[Sanskrit]** *śukladharma*: "White dharmas"—wholesome, virtuous qualities.

¹⁶ **[Sanskrit]** *Vaiśravaṇa*: The god of wealth (Kubera); one of the four great kings.

¹⁷ **[Sanskrit]** *bhadraghaṭa*: The "auspicious pot"—a wish-granting vessel in Indian mythology.


## Key Concepts

- **Śraddhā** (श्रद्धा): Faith, confidence, trust—the foundation of the path
- **Bodhicitta** (बोधिचित्त): The mind of awakening; the aspiration for Buddhahood for the sake of all
- **Kalyāṇamitra** (कल्याणमित्र): "Good friend"—a spiritual companion or teacher
- **Śukladharma** (शुक्लधर्म): "White dharmas"—wholesome, virtuous mental factors


## Soul-Check Hints for Blues Version

- The Ratnolkā quotation is a *chain of testimonies*—each line building on the last. Consider rendering as call-and-response or building rhythm.
- Faith here isn't blind belief—it's *trust grounded in experience*. Blues epistemology: "I believe because I've been there."
- The image of faith as "mother" and "guide" is powerful—maternal/ancestral wisdom
- Bodhicitta as "seed," "field," "sword," "axe"—rich metaphor territory


### Part 3: Types of Bodhicitta, Mañjuśrī's Vows, and the Bodhisattva Discipline


## The Four Causes of Bodhicitta

As taught in the Daśadharmakasūtra:¹

> "Here, son of good family, one abiding in the bodhisattva lineage who has not yet generated bodhicitta—when encouraged, informed, and urged by the Tathāgata or by the Tathāgata's disciples—generates the mind toward unsurpassed perfect awakening. This is the **first cause** of generating bodhicitta.
>
> Upon hearing the glories of awakening or of bodhicitta being proclaimed, one generates the mind toward unsurpassed perfect awakening. This is the **second cause**.
>
> Seeing beings without protector, without refuge, without shelter, without island,² and establishing compassionate mind, one generates the mind toward unsurpassed perfect awakening. This is the **third cause** of generating bodhicitta.
>
> Seeing the Tathāgata's complete perfection in all aspects and generating delight, one generates the mind toward unsurpassed perfect awakening. This is the **fourth cause**."


## Two Types of Bodhicitta

That bodhicitta is twofold: **bodhipraṇidhicitta** (aspiration-awakening-mind) and **bodhiprasthānacitta** (engagement-awakening-mind).³

As stated in the Āryagaṇḍavyūhasūtra:

> "Rare, son of good family, are those beings in all the world who set their mind on unsurpassed perfect awakening. Yet rarer still are those beings who have set forth toward unsurpassed perfect awakening."⁴

Therein, **bodhipraṇidhicitta** arises from the aspiration "I shall become a Buddha." 


## Even the Slightest Good Deed Matters

Even in the Śūragamasūtra it is stated that bodhicitta generated even through deceit becomes a cause of Buddhahood.⁵ How much more so when some wholesome deed is performed!

As stated in the Bhadrakalpikasūtra:⁶

> "The Tathāgata named Ghoṣadatta—it was there that the Tathāgata Nakṣatrarāja first generated bodhicitta by offering a betel leaf while he was a cowherd.
>
> The Tathāgata named Vidyutpradīpa—it was there that the Tathāgata Yaśas first generated bodhicitta by offering a shuttle while he was a weaver.
>
> The Tathāgata named Anantaprabha—it was there that the Tathāgata Arciṣmat first generated bodhicitta by offering a grass lamp while he was a city lamplighter.
>
> The Tathāgata named Dṛḍhavikrama—it was there that the Tathāgata Duṣpradharṣa first generated bodhicitta by offering a toothpick while he was a wood-gatherer."

And so forth.


## Even Imperfect Bodhicitta Must Not Be Despised

Even when bodhicitta is incomplete in practice, it must not be despised, since it produces infinite happiness throughout saṃsāra.

As described in the Āryamaitreyavimokṣa:⁷

> "Just as, son of good family, even a broken diamond gem surpasses all excellent gold ornaments, and does not lose the name 'diamond gem,' and turns back all poverty—so too, son of good family, even the diamond gem of generating the mind of omniscience, though broken in disposition and practice, surpasses the gold ornament of all śrāvaka and pratyekabuddha qualities, does not lose the name 'bodhicitta,' and turns back the poverty of all saṃsāra."


## The King's Practice: Bodhicitta Without Full Conduct

From this it should be known that bodhicitta is beneficial even without [full] conduct. As stated in the Aparārājāvavādakasūtra:⁸

> "Since, O great king, you have many duties and many responsibilities, and are unable to train completely at all times in the perfection of generosity... through to the perfection of wisdom... therefore, O great king, whether going, standing, sitting, lying down, awake, eating, or drinking—constantly and continually remember, establish in mind, and cultivate the desire for perfect awakening, faith, and aspiration.
>
> Having gathered, weighed, and combined all the roots of virtue of all Buddhas, bodhisattvas, pratyekabuddhas, noble śrāvakas, ordinary beings, and yourself in the three times—rejoice! Rejoice with the supreme rejoicing, up to equality with space, equality with nirvāṇa!
>
> Having rejoiced, dedicate it to the worship of all Buddhas, bodhisattvas, pratyekabuddhas, and noble śrāvakas. Having dedicated, make it common to all beings. Then, three times daily, dedicate toward unsurpassed perfect awakening for the attainment of omniscience by all beings and the fulfillment of all Buddha-dharmas.
>
> Thus practicing, O great king, you will rule the kingdom, you will not neglect the duties of kingship, and you will fulfill the accumulations for awakening."


## The Ripening of the King's Merit

And there too its ripening is stated:

> "You, O great king, through the ripening of that wholesome root-action of perfect awakening-mind, have been reborn among the gods hundreds of times. You have been reborn among humans hundreds of times. In all those divine and human rebirths, you exercise sovereignty alone.
>
> And, O great king, there is no diminishment or incompleteness apparent in that wholesome action of perfect awakening-mind. Moreover, O great king, even a single perfect awakening-mind, since it aims at the rescue of all beings, the liberation of all beings, the consolation of all beings, the parinirvāṇa of all beings—produces immeasurable, incalculable accumulation of virtue. How much more so when one cultivates it abundantly!"


## Mañjuśrī's Vows

This bodhicitta arises from seeing a form-body [of the Buddha].⁹ In the former birth-stories it is read... Thus aspiration-bodhicitta should be understood.

Now this must be said: Does one who has not entered the [bodhisattva] stages¹⁰ have the qualification for the bodhisattva vow or not? It should be known that they do...

As stated in the Āryamañjuśrībudddhakṣetraguṇavyūhālaṃkārasūtra,¹¹ the Blessed One, as Mañjuśrī in a former birth-story, generated bodhicitta endowed with practice. Thus should one generate it:

### Mañjuśrī's Aspiration Verses¹²

> **yāvatī prathamā koṭiḥ saṃsārasyāntavarjitā |**
> **tāvatsattvahitārthāya cariṣyāmyamitāṃ carim ||**

*"For as long as the first ten-million [eons] of saṃsāra endure without end, for that long shall I practice immeasurable conduct for the benefit of beings."*

> **utpādayāmi saṃbodhau cittaṃ nāthasya saṃmukham |**
> **nimantraye jagatsarvaṃ dāridryānmocitāsmi tat ||**

*"I generate the mind of awakening in the presence of the Protector. I invite the whole world—I shall free them from poverty."*

> **vyāpādakhilacittaṃ vā īrṣyāmātsaryameva vā |**
> **adyāgre na kariṣyāmi bodhiṃ prāpsyāmi yāvatā |**
> **brahmacaryaṃ cariṣyāmi kāmāṃstyakṣyāmi pāpakān ||**

*"Ill-will, a hardened mind, envy, or stinginess—from today forward I shall not produce them, until I attain awakening. I shall practice celibacy; I shall abandon evil desires."*

> **buddhānāmanuśikṣiṣye śīlasaṃvarasaṃyame |**
> **nāhaṃ tvaritarūpeṇa bodhiṃ prāptumihotsahe ||**

*"I shall train after the Buddhas in the discipline of ethical restraint. I do not strive to attain awakening here in haste."*

> **parāntakoṭiṃ sthāsyāmi sattvasyaikasya kāraṇāt |**
> **kṣetraṃ viśodhayiṣyāmi aprameyamacintiyam ||**

*"I shall remain until the final end of eons for the sake of even one being. I shall purify my buddha-field, immeasurable and inconceivable."*

> **nāmadheyaṃ kariṣyāmi daśadikṣu ca viśrutam |**
> **kāyavākkarmaṇī cāhaṃ śodhayiṣyāmi sarvaśaḥ |**
> **śodhayiṣye manaskarma karma kartāsmi nāśubham ||**

*"I shall make my name renowned in the ten directions. I shall purify my bodily and verbal actions completely. I shall purify my mental action; I shall not do evil deeds."*


## The Summary of Bodhisattva Training

This, in brief, is the body of bodhisattva training. In detail, however, it is an exposition that does not end even in immeasurable eons.

Or, in brief, there are two transgressions for a bodhisattva:¹³

1. **Undertaking without examining capacity**: If one undertakes what is appropriate or inappropriate to one's ability without examining, or does not desist or [wrongly] remains indifferent—one incurs transgression.

2. **Transgressing even when capable**: If, having examined and [knowing one is] capable, one transgresses nevertheless—even if prompted by a caṇḍāla slave¹⁴—one incurs transgression.


## The Great Fruit of Even Beginning Training

Whoever desires to practice this training should make effort here in the Śikṣāsamuccaya, learning at least the gateway of practice, since even beginning training has great fruit.

As stated in the Praśāntaviniścayaprātihāryasūtra:¹⁵

> "If, Mañjuśrī, a bodhisattva were to give to each Buddha, numbering as many as the sands of the Gaṅgā, buddha-fields equal in number to the sands of the Gaṅgā, filled with the great gem Vaśirāja—giving thus for kalpas equal to the sands of the Gaṅgā—
>
> Or if another bodhisattva, Mañjuśrī, having heard these kinds of dharmas, were to go to a secluded place and examine with the mind, 'I shall train in these kinds of dharmas'—
>
> That bodhisattva, Mañjuśrī, even though untrained, desiring this training, produces more merit. That merit of giving alone is not [equal to this]."


## Fearlessness in Face of Persecution

Therefore a bodhisattva who sees these benefits must never turn back. As stated there:

> "If, Mañjuśrī, there were beings as numerous as the dust atoms of a three-thousand-great-thousand world-system, and each one became a king, lord of Jambudvīpa, and they all proclaimed: 'Whoever takes up, holds, recites, masters, and propagates the Mahāyāna seal—we shall cause him to descend by cutting off his fingernails for a month, day by day, and by this method we shall kill him'—
>
> If, Mañjuśrī, a bodhisattva when thus addressed does not tremble, does not become afraid, does not fear even for a single mind-moment, does not despair, does not doubt, and moreover strives for embracing the true Dharma, abides devoted to study and recitation—
>
> That bodhisattva, Mañjuśrī, should be called 'hero of mind,' 'hero of giving,' 'hero of discipline,' 'hero of patience,' 'hero of energy,' 'hero of meditation,' 'hero of wisdom,' 'hero of samādhi.'
>
> If, Mañjuśrī, that bodhisattva does not become angry, does not feel hostility, does not produce a defiled mind toward those executioners—that bodhisattva, Mañjuśrī, is like Brahmā, like Indra, is unshakeable."


## Footnotes

¹ **[Source]** *Daśadharmakasūtra*: The "Sūtra of Ten Dharmas," providing four causes for generating bodhicitta.

² **[Sanskrit]** *anāthānatrāṇanaśaraṇānadvīpān*: "without protector, refuge, shelter, or island"—a powerful image of beings adrift in saṃsāra.

³ **[Philosophical]** The distinction between *praṇidhicitta* (aspiration-mind, "wishing" bodhicitta) and *prasthānacitta* (engagement-mind, "entering" bodhicitta) is fundamental to Mahāyāna ethics. Aspiration is like wanting to travel; engagement is actually setting out.

⁴ **[Cross-ref]** This passage is also quoted in Bodhicaryāvatāra 1.8-9.

⁵ **[Source]** *Śūragamasūtra*: The "Heroic Going Sūtra."

⁶ **[Source]** *Bhadrakalpikasūtra*: The "Sūtra of the Auspicious Eon," describing the thousand Buddhas of this kalpa.

⁷ **[Source]** *Maitreyavimokṣa*: The liberation chapter of the Gaṇḍavyūha featuring Maitreya.

⁸ **[Source]** *Aparārājāvavādakasūtra*: "Sūtra on Admonishing Another King"—a teaching on how busy householders can practice.

⁹ **[Sanskrit]** *rūpakāya*: The "form-body" of Buddha, as opposed to the dharma-body.

¹⁰ **[Philosophical]** *bhūmi*: The ten stages of bodhisattva development. The question is whether one must be on a stage to take bodhisattva vows.

¹¹ **[Source]** *Mañjuśrībudddhakṣetraguṇavyūhālaṃkārasūtra*: "Sūtra on the Ornaments and Qualities of Mañjuśrī's Buddha-field."

¹² **[Kārikā]** These verses are Mañjuśrī's original vows, quoted as models for aspiring bodhisattvas.

¹³ **[Philosophical]** This is a crucial summary of bodhisattva ethics: transgression comes either from (1) acting without knowing one's capacity, or (2) knowingly failing to act when capable.

¹⁴ **[Sanskrit]** *caṇḍāladāsa*: A "slave of the outcaste class"—the lowest possible social position. Even admonition from such a person should be heeded.

¹⁵ **[Source]** *Praśāntaviniścayaprātihāryasūtra*: "Sūtra on the Miraculous Display of Peaceful Certainty."


## Key Concepts

- **Bodhipraṇidhicitta** (बोधिप्रणिधिचित्त): Aspiration-bodhicitta—the wish to attain awakening
- **Bodhiprasthānacitta** (बोधिप्रस्थानचित्त): Engagement-bodhicitta—actually entering the path
- **Catvāri kāraṇāni** (चत्वारि कारणानि): The four causes of generating bodhicitta
- **Śūra** (शूर): Hero—the epithet for a fearless bodhisattva


## Soul-Check Hints for Blues Version

- Mañjuśrī's vows are *personal testimony*—"I will..." statements of commitment. Treat as Blues commitment/vow.
- The broken diamond image is powerful: even flawed bodhicitta outshines perfect self-centered virtue
- The King's practice shows that *everyone* can practice, regardless of circumstances
- The persecution passage has martyrdom energy—the willingness to suffer for the truth


### Part 4: The Core Summary, Self-Offering, and Dedication of Merit


## The Great Merit of Training

From the Candrapradīpasūtra:¹

> *One who serves tens of millions of koṭis of Buddhas*
> *with food and drink, with serene mind,*
> *with parasols, banners, and rows of lamps,*
> *for koṭis of kalpas like the sands of the Gaṅgā—*
>
> *And one who, when the true Dharma is fading,*
> *when the Sugata's teaching is ceasing,*
> *practices the training for one day and night—*
> *this produces merit more distinguished than that.*

Therefore, effort should be made here.


## The Bodhisattva Training Precepts

The bodhisattva training precepts have been stated in the sūtras. As stated in the Āryaratnamegha:²

> "How, son of good family, do bodhisattvas become restrained by the bodhisattva-training-vow? Here a bodhisattva reflects thus: 'By the mere prātimokṣa restraint I am not able to fully awaken to unsurpassed perfect awakening. Rather, I must train in those bodhisattva conduct-precepts that have been established by the Tathāgata in those various sūtras.'"

And so forth at length. Therefore, for those of dull intelligence like us, since it is difficult to know due to being extensively stated:

### Kārikā 3

> **marmasthānānyato vidyād yenānāpattiko bhavet ||3||**

*"Therefore one should know the vital points by which one becomes free of transgression."*³


## The Core Summary: Kārikā 4

What are those vital points that are stated in the sūtras for the benefit of those devoted to the Mahāyāna?

Namely:

### Kārikā 4

> **ātmabhāvasya bhogānāṃ tryadhvavṛtteḥ śubhasya ca |**
> **utsargaḥ sarvasattvebhyas tadrakṣā śuddhivardhanam ||4||**

*The relinquishment of one's own person,⁴ enjoyments, and merit accrued in the three times,⁵ to all beings; [and] the safeguarding of that [relinquishment] is purification and increase.*⁺

> **[Professor's Note]:** *This verse presents two distinct statements: (1) the three-fold giving (ātmabhāva, bhoga, śubha) to all beings, and (2) the protection of that act of giving as itself a means of purification and increase of merit. The dual-statement structure is essential to Śāntideva's rhetoric.*


## The Essence of the Bodhisattva Vow

This is the summary of the bodhisattva vow-restraint, in which transgressions are established even for bodhisattvas who pause in their practice.

As stated in the Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa:⁶

> "The path that the bodhisattva has taken up leads to the cessation of suffering for all beings. If, for a bodhisattva established on that path, even after the passing of ten million kalpas, a single thought of [personal] happiness should arise—even a thought of sitting down—the bodhisattva should generate this thought: 'Having taken up the urgent [welfare] of all beings, I sit down while abandoning even this [personal comfort].'"


## The Five Immediacies

Also Mañjuśrī said:

> "There are these five immediacies,⁷ Son of the Gods, endowed with which bodhisattvas swiftly fully awaken to unsurpassed perfect awakening. What are the five?
>
> 1. When, Son of the Gods, a bodhisattva generates the mind toward unsurpassed perfect awakening with sincere intention and does not in the meantime generate the mind toward the śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha stage—this, Son of the Gods, is the **first immediacy**.
>
> 2. Having generated the mind for the relinquishment of one's entire [being], one does not in the meantime associate with a stingy mind—this, Son of the Gods, is the **second immediacy**.
>
> 3. Having generated the thought 'All beings are to be protected by me,' one does not in the meantime sink down—this, Son of the Gods, is the **third immediacy**.
>
> 4. Having generated the thought 'I shall comprehend all dharmas as unarisen and unceasing,' one does not in the meantime fall into wrong views—this, Son of the Gods, is the **fourth immediacy**.
>
> 5. Having generated the thought 'Through wisdom united with a single moment, I shall comprehend all dharmas,' one does not in the meantime stand still, does not spit [on the path], until omniscience is attained—this, Son of the Gods, is the **fifth immediacy**."


## The Practice of Relinquishment

Therefore, the relinquishment, protection, purification, and increase of one's person, enjoyments, and merit should be cultivated as appropriate.

There, first, for the purpose of relinquishment, one should generate dispassion through the door of contemplating the faults of grasping, and should cultivate the benefits of giving.

As stated in the Candrapradīpasūtra:⁸

> *Those fools who are attached to this putrid body,*
> *to this unstable, powerless life like an illusion, like a dream—*
> *having done extremely terrible deeds, following the power of delusion,*
> *they go to terrible hells, unwise ones who have mounted the vehicle of death.*


## The Medicine Tree of the Body

As stated in the Anantamukhanirhāradhāraṇī:⁹

> *Whatever beings do not experience conflict—grasping is the root-cause of that.*
> *Therefore one should abandon wherever craving might arise; for one who has abandoned craving, there is dhāraṇī.*

As stated in the Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa:

> "Furthermore, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva generates the perception of 'belonging to another' in all dharmas. He does not grasp any phenomenon. Why? Because grasping is fear."

As stated in the Āryogradattaparipṛcchā:¹⁰

> "What is given no longer needs to be protected; what is in the house must be protected. What is given leads to the exhaustion of craving; what is in the house increases craving. What is given is without grasping; what is in the house is with grasping. What is given is without fear; what is in the house is with fear.
>
> What is given supports the path to awakening; what is in the house supports Māra. What is given is imperishable; what is in the house perishes. From what is given comes happiness; from what is in the house, suffering arises. What is given is for the abandonment of afflictions; what is in the house increases afflictions. What is given leads to great enjoyment; what is in the house does not. What is given is the deed of a good person; what is in the house is the deed of a bad person. What is given is praised by all Buddhas; what is in the house is praised by fools."


## Giving Even the Body

From the Nārāyaṇaparipṛcchā:¹¹

> "That thing should not be taken up in which the mind of giving does not arise. The intention of giving should not proceed [stuck]. That possession should not be taken up in which the mind of relinquishment does not arise...
>
> Moreover, son of good family, the bodhisattva mahāsattva should generate this thought: 'This my person has been given up, relinquished to all beings—how much more external things!
>
> Whatever being needs whatever from me, I shall give that to them when present. I shall give my hand to those who need a hand, my foot to those who need a foot, my eye to those who need an eye, my flesh to those who need flesh, my blood to those who need blood, my marrow to those who need marrow, my limbs to those who need limbs, my head to those who need a head.
>
> How much more external things—wealth, grain, gold, silver, gems, ornaments, horses, elephants, chariots, vehicles, villages, cities, towns, districts, kingdoms, capitals, ports, slaves male and female, workers, servants, sons, daughters, and retinue!'"


## The Medicine Tree Metaphor

> "Just as, son of good family, when a medicine tree¹² is taken from—whether from its root, trunk, branch, bark, leaf, flower, fruit, or essence—it has no discrimination: 'It is taken from my root' up to 'It is taken from my essence.' Rather, without discrimination it removes the diseases of beings low, middling, and excellent.
>
> Just so, son of good family, the bodhisattva mahāsattva should generate the perception of medicine in this very body made of the four great elements. Whatever beings need whatever, let them take it from me—hand for those who need a hand, foot for those who need a foot..."


## Dedication of Merit

As stated in the Āryagaganagañjasūtra:¹³

> "May that root of virtue of mine, that Dharma-knowledge, that skill, not exist that would not be for the benefit of all beings."


## Dedication of Past and Future Merit

As stated in the Āryākṣayamatisūtra:¹⁴

> "The recollection of wholesome mental factors and, having recollected, their dedication to awakening—this is skill regarding the past. The intention toward future wholesome roots, the cultivation of facing toward awakening, [thinking:] 'Those wholesome mind-moments that will arise in me, I shall dedicate them to unsurpassed perfect awakening'—this is skill regarding the future."


## Chapter Conclusion

Thus, through mental practice of complete relinquishment, having fulfilled relinquishment through the impetus of the mind of giving, by that physical activity all possessions are relinquished. Freed from the suffering of existence rooted in possessions, one is called "liberated."

And one experiences immeasurable, incalculable kalpas of diverse, infinite mundane and supramundane showers of happiness. And by that very person and so forth, like a hook with bait, drawing others while oneself not having obtained the enjoyment,¹⁵ one ferries them across.

Therefore it is stated in the Ratnamegha:

> **"For the bodhisattva, giving (dāna) is awakening (bodhi)."**¹⁶


*Thus ends the First Chapter, the Perfection of Generosity, in the Śikṣāsamuccaya.*


## Footnotes

¹ **[Source]** *Candrapradīpasūtra*: The "Moon Lamp Sūtra."

² **[Source]** *Āryaratnamegha*: The "Noble Cloud of Jewels Sūtra."

³ **[Kārikā]** Root verse 3 of the Śikṣāsamuccayakārikā.

⁴ **[Sanskrit]** *ātmabhāva*: Literally "self-existence"—one's own person, body, life.

⁵ **[Sanskrit]** *tryadhvavṛtti*: "Occurring in the three times"—past, present, and future merit.

⁶ **[Source]** *Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa*: The bodhisattva liberation discipline.

⁷ **[Sanskrit]** *ānantarya*: "Immediacy"—here a positive term meaning actions that lead directly to awakening (cf. the negative "five immediacies" that lead to hell).

⁸ **[Cross-ref]** This verse emphasizes the impurity and impermanence of the body as motivation for giving.

⁹ **[Source]** *Anantamukhanirhāradhāraṇī*: "Dhāraṇī of Producing Infinite Gateways."

¹⁰ **[Source]** *Ugradattaparipṛcchā*: "Questions of Ugradatta."

¹¹ **[Source]** *Nārāyaṇaparipṛcchā*: "Questions of Nārāyaṇa."

¹² **[Sanskrit]** *bhaiṣajyavṛkṣa*: The "medicine tree"—a powerful metaphor for the bodhisattva body given for the healing of all.

¹³ **[Source]** *Gaganagañjasūtra*: "Jewel of Space Sūtra."

¹⁴ **[Source]** *Ākṣayamatisūtra*: "Sūtra of Inexhaustible Intention."

¹⁵ **[Philosophical]** The paradox: by giving away everything, the bodhisattva draws beings to liberation—yet the giving itself is selfless.

¹⁶ **[Key Statement]** The summary of Chapter 1: *dānaṃ hi bodhisattvasya bodhiḥ*—"For the bodhisattva, giving is awakening itself."


## Key Concepts

- **Marmasthāna** (मर्मस्थान): "Vital points"—the essential summary of bodhisattva training
- **Ātmabhāvotsarga** (आत्मभावोत्सर्ग): Relinquishment of one's person/body
- **Ānantarya** (आनन्तर्य): Immediacy—actions leading directly to awakening
- **Bhaiṣajyavṛkṣa** (भैषज्यवृक्ष): The medicine tree—metaphor for the giving body


## Soul-Check Hints for Blues Version

- Kārikā 4 is the **essence of the whole text**—must be rendered with weight
- The medicine tree metaphor is extraordinary: "Take what you need from me"
- "Given vs. kept" antitheses are perfect for Blues call-and-response
- The final statement: "Giving IS awakening" = Blues liberation




---



<div id='chapter-2'></div>

# Chapter 2: Embracing the True Dharma (Saddharmaparigraha)

---

*The second chapter of Śāntideva's Compendium of Training, on the protection and preservation of the true Dharma.*

---

## Introduction: The Protection of What Is Given

Thus, even when one's person, enjoyments, and merit have been relinquished,¹ they must still be protected.² Why? Because:

### Kārikā 5

> **paribhogāya sattvānāmātmabhāvādi dīyate |**
> **arakṣite kuto bhogaḥ kiṃ dattaṃ yanna bhujyate ||5||**

*"One's person and so forth are given for the enjoyment of beings; if unprotected, how can there be enjoyment? What gift is it that is not consumed [by them]?"*³

Therefore, one should protect one's person and so forth for the sake of beings' enjoyment.

---

## The Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa Teaching

As stated in the Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa:⁴

> "Furthermore, Śāriputra, [thinking] 'I shall protect another,' the self must be protected. Endowed with such benevolent intention, Śāriputra, the bodhisattva does not do evil action even for the sake of [preserving] life."

---

## The Vīradattaparipṛcchā Teaching

In the Vīradattaparipṛcchā it is also stated:⁵

> "Śakaṭamitra, [the body] should be borne only with the intention of Dharma, for the sake of carrying the burden."

Likewise, in the Akṣayamatisūtra:⁶

> "One is not wearied by bodily suffering because of consideration for beings."

---

## Protection Through Spiritual Friends

How, then, should one protect one's person and so forth? **Through not abandoning spiritual friends** (*kalyāṇamitrānutsarga*).⁷

As stated in the Āryagaṇḍavyūha by the noble Śrīsaṃbhava:⁸

> "Bodhisattvas upheld by spiritual friends, O son of good family, do not fall into bad rebirths. Bodhisattvas attended upon by spiritual friends do not transgress the bodhisattva training. Bodhisattvas sheltered by spiritual friends rise above the world. Bodhisattvas served by spiritual friends become unforgetful in all bodhisattva practices. Bodhisattvas embraced by spiritual friends become invincible by karma and defilements.
>
> Spiritual friends are instructors: they restrain one from what should not be done, from places of heedlessness. They are those who lead one out from the city of saṃsāra.
>
> Therefore, O son of good family, with such mental orientation, one should approach spiritual friends with relaxed confidence:
>
> With a mind like **the earth**, in order to bear all burdens;
> With a mind like **a diamond**, in unbreakable intention;
> With a mind like **a mountain range**, in not trembling before any suffering;
> With a mind like **a servant of the world**, in not disdaining undertaking all tasks;
> With a mind like **a dust-cloth**, in abandoning arrogance and pride;
> With a mind like **a vehicle**, in carrying heavy loads;
> With a mind like **a dog**, in not becoming angry;
> With a mind like **a boat**, in not being troubled by going and coming;
> Like **a good son**, in gazing upon the face of spiritual friends.
>
> And in yourself, O son of good family, you should generate the perception of being **sick**; in spiritual friends, the perception of **physicians**; in their instructions, the perception of **medicine**; in practice, the perception of **curing the disease**.
>
> And in yourself, O son of good family, you should generate the perception of being **fearful**; in spiritual friends, the perception of **heroes**; in their instructions, the perception of **weapons**; in practice, the perception of **destroying enemies**."

---

## The Acalopāsikā Testimony

In the same [Gaṇḍavyūha], in the liberation of the lay-woman Acalā, it is stated:⁹

> "For a bodhisattva, O son of good family, who practices the instructions of spiritual friends, the blessed Buddhas become of pleased mind. For a bodhisattva who stands in conformity with the words of spiritual friends, omniscience draws near. For one who has no doubt regarding the words of spiritual friends, spiritual friends draw near. For one whose mental attention is never separated from spiritual friends, all purposes come face to face."

---

## Sudhana's Devotion

For this very reason, the noble Sudhana,¹⁰ having prostrated at the feet of the monk Sāradhvaja with his head, having circumambulated him hundreds of thousands of times, looking upon him, bowing down, looking again and again, certainly prostrating, paying homage, bending low, taking to mind, reflecting, contemplating, thoroughly contemplating, giving utterances of joy, making exclamations of "hā!", bringing to mind his qualities, completing remembrance, stabilizing memory, not abandoning, mentally drawing near, fastening his aspiration, immersing himself in the vision, grasping the sign of his presence—thus he departed from his presence.

Likewise, seeing omniscience as having come from spiritual friends, with tearful face, weeping, he departed from the presence of Megha the Dramiḍa.¹¹

---

## The Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa on Dharma-Desire

In the Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa it is also stated:¹²

> "Here, Śāriputra, through desire for the Dharma, there is no treasure in the world that the bodhisattva does not relinquish. There is no bodily service that he does not perform. There is no errand on foot that he will not undertake. There is no verbal action that he will not undertake, out of respect for teachers and preceptors. And so on at length.
>
> For what reason? This Dharma conduces to the cutting of bonds. This Dharma conduces to the cutting of birth, old age, sickness, death, sorrow, lamentation, suffering, and mental distress.
>
> Having generated the thought [of the Dharma] as a jewel, having generated the thought of medicine, [thinking:] 'This Dharma conduces to the pacification of the affliction of all beings'—and: 'We must seek such a Dharma for the pacification of the affliction of all beings.'"

---

## The Ugradattaparipṛcchā on Teacher-Reverence

In the Ugradattaparipṛcchā it is also stated:¹³

> "Moreover, householder, if a bodhisattva who is desirous of recitation and study hears from someone a four-line verse, or has it pointed out, or learns it—connected with giving, morality, patience, effort, meditation, or wisdom, or connected with the accumulation of bodhisattva provisions—then for that teacher he should show reverence for the Dharma commensurate with however many name-words and syllables are in the verse so pointed out.
>
> If he were to perform service and attendance upon that teacher for that many eons, without deceit, with all gain, honor, and worship—even then, householder, the reverence for the teacher would not yet be fulfilled. How much less the reverence for the Dharma!"

---

## The Story of Sadāprarudita: Part One

In the Aṣṭasāhasrikā Prajñāpāramitā it is also stated:¹⁴

> "Therefore, O son of good family, intense reverence should be generated toward spiritual friends, and love should be shown.
>
> Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita,¹⁵ proceeding with such qualities of reverent mental attention, gradually reached a certain city. There, having entered the middle of the marketplace, this thought occurred to him: 'I will sell this very body of mine, and with that price I will make offerings to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Dharmodgata.¹⁶ For a long time, my thousands of bodies have been broken, exhausted, sold away. Again, in the immeasurable saṃsāra, I have experienced immeasurable [sufferings] for the sake of desire, with desire as cause. But not for such Dharmas, nor for the offering of such beings!'
>
> Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita, having entered the middle of the marketplace, raised his voice and proclaimed: 'Who wants a man? Who wants a man? Who wants a man?'
>
> Then Māra the Evil One so arranged the brahmins and householders that they did not hear that cry. When he could not find a buyer for himself, having gone aside, he began to weep and shed tears, speaking thus: 'Alas, what misfortune for us, that we cannot find even a buyer for our own body!'
>
> Then Śakra, lord of the gods, in the form of a young brahmin, approached the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita and said: 'Why are you, O son of good family, standing here with downcast face and anxious heart, shedding tears?'
>
> Sadāprarudita said: 'Young brahmin, I wish to sell this very body of mine out of desire for the Dharma, in order to make Dharma-offering. And I cannot find a buyer for it.'
>
> And so on at length.
>
> Then that young brahmin said to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita: 'I have no need of a man, O son of good family. But my father has a sacrifice to perform. For that I need a man's heart, blood, and bone-marrow. Will you give [these] for a price?'
>
> Then this thought occurred to Sadāprarudita: 'What gain I have obtained! And I know myself to be accomplished in the skill in means of Prajñāpāramitā, in that I have found a buyer for myself—for my heart, blood, and bone-marrow!'
>
> With joyful mind, glad mind, delighted mind, he said to that young brahmin: 'I will give you, young brahmin, whatever you want from this body of mine.'
>
> Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita, taking a sharp weapon, pierced his right arm and let the blood flow. And having pierced his right thigh and made it fleshless, he approached the foot of a wall to extract the bone."

---

## The Story of Sadāprarudita: Part Two

> "Then a certain merchant's daughter, from the upper terrace of her mansion, saw the bodhisattva Sadāprarudita. She approached him and said: 'What are you, O son of good family, doing to yourself in this manner?'
>
> And so on. Having heard the purpose of the offering, she said again: 'What kind of benefit will arise for you from that?'
>
> He said to her: 'That son of good family will teach me the Prajñāpāramitā and skill in means. There we shall train. Training there, we shall become a refuge for all beings.'
>
> And so on at length.
>
> Then that merchant's daughter said to the bodhisattva Sadāprarudita: 'How wonderful, O son of good family! Such noble and excellent Dharmas have been proclaimed by you! For the sake of even one such Dharma, O son of good family, bodies equal in number to the sands of the Ganges River should be given up, throughout eons. So noble and excellent are these Dharmas proclaimed by you!
>
> But, O son of good family, I will give you whatever you need—gold, gems, pearls, lapis lazuli, and so on—by which you may make offerings to the bodhisattva Dharmodgata.'"
>
> And so on, at length, until she, attended by five hundred maidens, makes the journey to him.¹⁷

---

## The Seven-Year Meditation

> "Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Dharmodgata, rising from his seat, entered his own house. For seven years he remained absorbed in a single samādhi.¹⁸
>
> For seven years the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita did not generate a thought of sense-desire, did not generate a thought of ill-will, did not generate a thought of harm, did not generate greed for tastes—except: 'When will the bodhisattva mahāsattva Dharmodgata arise? We shall prepare a Dharma-seat for him where he will sit and teach the Dharma. And we shall sprinkle that patch of ground, sweep it, and scatter it with various flowers.'
>
> Those five hundred maidens, headed by the merchant's daughter, learning from the bodhisattva Sadāprarudita, passed the time in only two postures.¹⁹
>
> Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita heard a divine utterance: 'Seven days from now, the bodhisattva mahāsattva Dharmodgata will arise from this samādhi and, sitting in the middle of the city, will teach the Dharma.'
>
> Then, having heard that utterance, the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita, joyful, delighted, filled with gladness and happiness of mind, cleaned that patch of ground. Together with the five hundred maidens headed by the merchant's daughter, he prepared a Dharma-seat made of the seven jewels.
>
> Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita, wishing to sprinkle that patch of ground, could not find water anywhere, searching all around. For Māra the Evil One had made all the water disappear, [thinking:] 'Perhaps, not finding water, his mind will become distressed, or grief will arise, or there will be some change of mind, by which his roots of virtue will disappear or not shine forth.'
>
> Then this thought occurred to the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita: 'What if I were to pierce my own body and sprinkle this ground with my blood? For what reason? This patch of ground is dusty. May the dust not fall upon the body of the bodhisattva mahāsattva Dharmodgata. What would I do with this body that is certainly subject to destruction anyway? Better that this body of mine perish through such action than through powerless action. For the sake of desire, with desire as cause, my thousands of bodies have been broken again and again in the immeasurable saṃsāra while wandering. If they are to be broken, let them rather be broken for such a Dharma-circumstance!'"

---

## The Blood-Offering

> "Then the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita, having reflected thus, taking a sharp weapon, pierced his own body all around and sprinkled that entire patch of ground with his own blood. Likewise did those maidens also.
>
> Yet there was no change of mind for the bodhisattva mahāsattva Sadāprarudita or for all those maidens, by which Māra the Evil One might have found an opening."²⁰

---

## Never Abandon Spiritual Friends

Thus it is also stated in the Caturdharmakasūtra:²¹

> "Bhikṣus, a spiritual friend should not be abandoned by a bodhisattva for as long as one lives—not even for the sake of [preserving] life."

Thus indeed:

### Kārikā 6

> **kalyāṇamitrānutsargāt**
> **ātmabhāvādīnāṃ rakṣādikaṃ kāryam |**
> **sūtrāṇāṃ ca sadekṣaṇāt ||6||**

*"Through not abandoning spiritual friends, and through constant examination of the sūtras, the protection and so forth of one's person and the rest should be accomplished."*²²

---

## The Sūtras as Authority

For the bodhisattva training-rules are for the most part seen in the sūtras themselves.²³ Because of the statement: "In each of those sūtrāntas, the bodhisattva conduct, the bodhisattva training-rules, are prescribed."

Therefore, lest there be transgression through not examining them, and lest one who has transgressed remain unrestrained through ignorance—constant attention should be given to seeing the sūtras.

By this—through not abandoning spiritual friends and through seeing the sūtrāntas—all embracing of the true Dharma has been stated.

---

## The Sāgaramatisūtra Definition

As stated in the Āryasāgaramatisūtra:²⁴

> "By whatever syllables and etymologies that inexpressible Dharma is indicated, the teaching that is the support of those syllables and etymologies—as far as this, it is called embracing the true Dharma.
>
> Furthermore, O son of good family, those Dharma-preachers who are teachers of such sūtrāntas and who have practice as their essence—the serving, cherishing, attending, rising for, waiting upon, revering, honoring, listening to, protecting, and embracing of those Dharma-preachers; the giving of robes, alms-food, bedding, seats, and medicines for the sick; the giving of praise; protection of their reputation; protection of their wholesome qualities; praise-speaking and concealment of blame—this too is embracing the true Dharma.
>
> And so on at length.
>
> Furthermore, O son of good family, devotion to non-disputation, and the defeat through Dharma of those who speak wrongly about what is not Dharma—this too is embracing the true Dharma.
>
> Furthermore, O son of good family, for one of unobstructed continuity, of intellect intent on liberating all beings, of mind without material reward, the gift of Dharma to others—this too is embracing the true Dharma.
>
> Furthermore, O son of good family, even a single step taken for the sake of hearing the Dharma or for teaching the Dharma, even a single inhalation and exhalation—this too is embracing the true Dharma.
>
> And so on at length.
>
> This mind, O son of good family, rushes toward sense-objects. Its restraint, protection, one-pointedness, training, calming, pacification, discipline—this is called embracing the true Dharma.
>
> And so on at length.
>
> Furthermore, O son of good family, the non-grasping and non-attachment to a dharma through which adharma operates—this too is embracing the true Dharma."
>
> And so on.

---

## The Indispensability of Dharma-Embracing

In this [passage], through serving Dharma-preachers and so forth, not abandoning spiritual friends is taught, as well as the mark of a spiritual friend.²⁵

By this: without this embracing of the true Dharma, there is no protection, no purification, no increase. And therefore one is not a bodhisattva either.

**Therefore, embracing the true Dharma is entirely necessary.**

---

## The Śrīmālāsiṃhanādasūtra Teaching

As stated in the Śrīmālāsiṃhanādasūtra:²⁶

> "Whatever numerous bodhisattva vows there are, O Blessed One, equal to the sands of the Ganges River—all are deposited in one great vow, are included in it, are established upon it: namely, in embracing the true Dharma.
>
> Of such great scope, O Blessed One, is embracing the true Dharma."

---

## The Blow to Māra

Again in the same [sūtra] it is stated:²⁷

> "Just as, O goddess, even a small blow to a vulnerable spot is painful and injurious even for a person of great strength—just so, O goddess, even a little embracing of the true Dharma is painful to Māra the Evil One, is a cause of sorrow, is productive of lamentation.
>
> I do not see, O goddess, any other single wholesome dharma that is so painful to Māra the Evil One, so grief-causing, so lamentation-producing, as even this little embracing of the true Dharma."

---

## Greater Than Mount Sumeru

Again it is stated:²⁸

> "Just as, O goddess, Mount Sumeru, king of mountains, surpassing all the subsidiary mountains, shines forth and shines well through its height and breadth—just so, O goddess, the embracing of the true Dharma by a Mahāyānist who is heedless of body and life and who does not have a grasping mind surpasses all the wholesome dharmas even of those Mahāyānists newly set out [on the path], who are heedful of body and life."
>
> And so on.

---

## The Benefits Enumerated in Verse

Likewise in the Āryasāgaramatisūtra it is also stated:²⁹

> *Embraced is one by the Victors,*
> *by gods, nāgas, and kinnaras.*
> *Embraced by merit and knowledge—*
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.* (...and so on...)
>
> *One is never born in empty fields;*
> *in every birth one sees the Victor.*
> *Seeing him, one gains serene faith—*
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.*
>
> *One becomes a great being who remembers past lives,*
> *again and again obtaining the going forth [into homelessness].*
> *[One becomes] pure in conduct, with practice as essence—*
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.* (...and so on...)
>
> *One becomes skilled and obtains dhāraṇī;*
> *the good does not perish through hundreds of eons.*
> *One becomes eloquent and unattached—*
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.*
>
> *Śakra, Brahmā, and the world-protectors,*
> *a human king, a wheel-turning monarch on earth—*
> *with ease and happiness one awakens to enlightenment—*
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.*
>
> *Thirty-two marks appear upon one's body;*
> *one becomes blameless of limb and discerning.*
> *Those gazing upon one find no satisfaction—*³⁰
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.*
>
> *One's awakening-mind does not become confused;*
> *nor is one uplifted in the practice of perfections.*
> *Skillful among hundreds, one is not led astray—*
> *[through] upholding the true Dharma of the Tathāgatas.*

---

*Thus ends the Second Chapter, Embracing the True Dharma, in the Śikṣāsamuccaya, [found] within the Perfection of Morality.*³¹

---

## Footnotes

¹ **[Cross-ref]** Reference to Chapter 1's teaching on the relinquishment of *ātmabhāva*, *bhoga*, and *śubha*.

² **[Sanskrit]** *rakṣā*: Protection, safeguarding—the second aspect after *utsarga* (relinquishment).

³ **[Kārikā]** Root verse 5 establishes the necessity of protection. The logic: if you give something for others' enjoyment but fail to protect it, the gift is ineffectual.

⁴ **[Source]** *Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa*: The bodhisattva liberation discipline, cited extensively by Śāntideva.

⁵ **[Source]** *Vīradattaparipṛcchā*: "Questions of Vīradatta."

⁶ **[Source]** *Akṣayamatisūtra*: "Sūtra of Inexhaustible Intention."

⁷ **[Key Concept]** *Kalyāṇamitrānutsarga*: Non-abandonment of spiritual friends. This becomes the central theme of Chapter 2.

⁸ **[Source]** *Āryagaṇḍavyūha*: The Flower Ornament Sūtra's teaching on Śrīsaṃbhava, a spiritual friend met by Sudhana on his pilgrimage.

⁹ **[Source]** *Acalopāsikāvimokṣa*: The liberation attained through the lay-woman Acalā (also from the Gaṇḍavyūha).

¹⁰ **[Sanskrit]** *Sudhana*: The young pilgrim of the Gaṇḍavyūha, who visits 52 spiritual teachers. His devotion is the model for all practitioners.

¹¹ **[Source]** *Megha Dramiḍa*: Another of Sudhana's teachers. His name means "Cloud the Dravidian."

¹² **[Source]** *Bodhisattvaprātimokṣa*: The same text cited earlier; this passage emphasizes the "Dharma as jewel" and "Dharma as medicine" perceptions.

¹³ **[Source]** *Ugradattaparipṛcchā*: Emphasizing that even lifetimes of service cannot repay the debt owed to a teacher of a single verse.

¹⁴ **[Source]** *Aṣṭasāhasrikā Prajñāpāramitā*: The 8,000-line Perfection of Wisdom Sūtra, containing the famous story of Sadāprarudita.

¹⁵ **[Sanskrit]** *Sadāprarudita*: "Ever-Weeping"—named for his constant weeping from devotion to finding a teacher of Prajñāpāramitā.

¹⁶ **[Sanskrit]** *Dharmodgata*: "Dharma-Exalted"—the teacher whom Sadāprarudita seeks across the story.

¹⁷ **[Source]** The merchant's daughter and her 500 maidens join Sadāprarudita's pilgrimage, a model of collective devotion.

¹⁸ **[Sanskrit]** *Ekasamādhisamāpanna*: Absorbed in a single samādhi—a state of profound meditative concentration.

¹⁹ **[Philosophical]** "Only two postures": Walking and standing, meaning they never sat or lay down for seven years—a mark of extreme dedication.

²⁰ **[Philosophical]** *Avatāra*: "Opening" or "entry point"—Māra could not find any weakness in their minds to exploit.

²¹ **[Source]** *Caturdharmakasūtra*: "Sūtra of Four Dharmas"—a short text on essential bodhisattva practices.

²² **[Kārikā]** Root verse 6 summarizes the two methods of protection: reliance on spiritual friends and constant study of sūtras.

²³ **[Philosophical]** Śāntideva's justification for his anthology method: the training rules are already in the sūtras; he merely compiles them.

²⁴ **[Source]** *Āryasāgaramatisūtra*: "Sūtra of the Noble Ocean-Mind"—one of Śāntideva's most frequently cited texts.

²⁵ **[Key Concept]** *Kalyāṇamitralakṣaṇa*: The characteristics that define a true spiritual friend.

²⁶ **[Source]** *Śrīmālāsiṃhanādasūtra*: "Sūtra of Queen Śrīmālā's Lion's Roar"—taught by a queen, emphasizing the one great vow.

²⁷ **[Philosophical]** Even small Dharma-practice wounds Māra—a striking image of spiritual warfare.

²⁸ **[Philosophical]** Dharma-embracing is higher than Mount Sumeru if done with heedlessness of body and life.

²⁹ **[Source]** The concluding verses from the Sāgaramatisūtra enumerate the benefits of Dharma-upholding.

³⁰ **[Poetic]** "No satisfaction": The Buddha's body is so beautiful that no one tires of looking upon it.

³¹ **[Structure]** This chapter falls within the *śīlapāramitā* (perfection of morality) section of the Śikṣāsamuccaya.

---

## Key Concepts

- **Saddharmaparigraha** (सद्धर्मपरिग्रह): Embracing/upholding the true Dharma
- **Kalyāṇamitra** (कल्याणमित्र): Spiritual friend, virtuous friend
- **Kalyāṇamitrānutsarga** (कल्याणमित्रानुत्सर्ग): Non-abandonment of spiritual friends
- **Sadāprarudita** (सदाप्ररुदित): "Ever-Weeping"—the model devotee
- **Dharmodgata** (धर्मोद्गत): "Dharma-Exalted"—the model teacher
- **Sūtrāntadarśana** (सूत्रान्तदर्शन): Examination/seeing of the sūtras

---

## Soul-Check Hints for Blues Version

- **The Sadāprarudita story is extraordinary**: Selling his body, piercing himself, seven years standing/walking
- **Spiritual friends as essential**: Not optional, not nice-to-have—*necessary*
- **"Even a breath for the Dharma"**: Even one step, one breath counts as Dharma-embracing
- **The mind like a servant/dog/dust-cloth**: Radical humility before teachers
- **Māra's wound**: Even tiny Dharma-practice hurts the Evil One




---



<div id='chapter-3'></div>

# Chapter 3: Protection of Dharma-Preachers and Others (Dharmabhāṇakādirakṣā)

---

*The third chapter of Śāntideva's Compendium of Training, on protecting Dharma-teachers and avoiding the various harms that assail the bodhisattva's path.*

---

## Introduction: The General Method of Protection

The method of protection and so forth for all three [i.e., person, enjoyments, merit] has been stated in general. Now the particulars of protection must be explained.¹

### Kārikā 7

> **tatrātmabhāve kā rakṣā yadanarthavivarjanam |**

*"Therein, what is the protection of one's person? It is the avoidance of harm."*²

Here, "therein" refers to one who abides in the embracing of the true Dharma [from Chapter 2]. The protection of one's person is to be considered as how one does not destroy others.³

---

## Part I: The Vow of the Dharma-Holders

This teaching on the avoidance of harm was spoken by bodhisattvas devoted to upholding the true Dharma in the Āryagaganagañjasūtra:⁴

> "We venture, O Blessed One, after the extinction of the Foremost Among Bipeds,
> We shall uphold the true Dharma, having abandoned body and life.
>
> Having relinquished gain and honor, having cast off all praise,
> Not relinquishing this Dharma that reveals the Buddha's wisdom.
>
> Abuse and harsh criticism, and words of ill-speaking—
> Through patience we shall endure them, for the sake of embracing the true Dharma.
>
> Raised fists and threats, and defamation and disgrace—
> All these we shall endure, upholding this method...
>
> In such a dreadful time of great danger, when monks are in want and distressed,
> In the time of devastation for beings, we shall uphold the true Dharma.
>
> Those profound sūtrāntas connected with the fruit of liberation—
> Those who accept them will not break; they will brush aside confused talk...
>
> Loving-kindness we shall practice toward those who are not established in the Dharma,
> And compassion we shall practice, upholding this method.
>
> Having seen beings of bad conduct, established in desire and greed,
> We shall shed tears—for where will such ones be reborn?
>
> And having seen just such an obstructor of the true Dharma,
> We shall befriend him from afar, lest he become angry with us.
>
> We shall protect as we are able, restrained in speech and action,
> We shall not suddenly address those who are established in their own evil.
>
> With gifts and also with respect, we shall ripen such persons here;
> And we shall urge them toward truth, away from the domain of evil.
>
> Having abandoned household production, wandering in the edges of the wilderness,
> We shall be like deer—with few concerns, with few tasks...
>
> Tamed, peaceful, and liberated, and having descended into a village,
> We shall teach the Dharma to beings who are seekers of Dharma.
>
> Even far we shall go, having heard of those who desire the Dharma,
> Having attained the delight in the Dharma-garden, we shall accomplish the welfare of the embodied.
>
> Having seen face to face the abundant stumbling of beings,
> We shall be self-observant, established in kindness toward the Dharma.
>
> Whether dishonored or honored, like Mount Meru established,
> Untainted by the world, we shall become guides for the world.
>
> Having heard the censure of monks whose conduct has split,
> We shall mind our own actions—may their karma not ripen [for us].
>
> They will hire assassins for those who abide in these dharmas—
> 'These dharmas are nowhere to be found among us!'
>
> 'Our śramaṇas have no śramaṇa qualities!'—
> Having heard true accusation, they reject this sūtra.
>
> For those whose ears and noses are cut off, how is a mirror pleasing?
> Having heard true accusation, they reject the true Dharma.
>
> Those monks who will embrace the true Dharma—
> They will strive so that someone may hear this Dharma.
>
> Kings will seize them, and great multitudes will break them;
> Through the Buddha's empowerment, beings will then hear this Dharma.
>
> In that harsh time, we, having abandoned body and life,
> Shall uphold the true Dharma, for the sake of beings' welfare."

---

## Part II: The Saddharmapuṇḍarīka Teaching

In the Āryasaddharmapuṇḍarīka it is also stated:⁵

> "One should protect one's conduct and sphere of activity; one should be unassociated and pure.
> One should always avoid intimacy with princes and kings.
>
> And also with the men of kings—one should not be intimate with them;
> With outcasts, boxers, drunkards, and all manner of sectarians.
>
> One should not serve those who are conceited, [even if] established in Vinaya and Āgama,
> Monks thought to be arhats—but the ill-conducted one should be avoided.
>
> The bhikṣuṇī should always be avoided whose sphere is laughter and gossip;
> And the upāsikās who are exposed and unsettled should be avoided.
>
> Women and hermaphrodites—intimacy with them should be avoided;
> And in households, young brides and maidens should be avoided.
>
> One should never befriend them or ask them 'How are you?' skillfully;
> And intimacy should be avoided with pig-dealers and sheep-dealers.
>
> Those who support women—intimacy with them should be avoided;
> With actors, jugglers, wrestlers, and all such people.
>
> One should not serve courtesans or others who live by entertainment;
> Greeting such persons should be entirely avoided.
>
> And when the wise one teaches the Dharma to women,
> One should not enter alone there, nor should one indulge in laughter."

---

## Part III: The Works of Māra

This is another harm that there would be—namely, what is called the work of Māra, stated in the Prajñāpāramitā:⁶

> "Māra the Evil One will zealously exert great effort near the bodhisattva who has recently set out in the Vehicle."

Here also it is said:⁷

> "Furthermore, Ānanda, at whatever time a bodhisattva mahāsattva applies himself to the Prajñāpāramitā, at that time the Māras, the Evil Ones, bring forth harassment of the bodhisattva; they generate fear.
>
> They let loose and display meteor-falls and conflagrations in all directions, [thinking:] 'Perhaps this bodhisattva mahāsattva will become discouraged, or perhaps his hair will stand on end!'—by which even one of his thought-moments might be diminished regarding supreme perfect enlightenment.
>
> Furthermore, others of different awareness will write [it] down... [and] acquire it. [Saying:] 'We are not obtaining any taste from this!'—they will rise from their seats and depart. Thus yawning, laughing... they will acquire it. This is the work of Māra.
>
> Thus, thoughts about the countryside, villages, and so forth will arise. Thus, mental attention to teachers, preceptors, mothers, fathers, friends, ministers, relatives, and blood-relations [will arise]. Thus, mental attention to thieves [will arise]. Thus, mental attention to robes and so forth [will arise].
>
> Furthermore, the Dharma-preacher will be eager to have someone copy, or recite, this profound Prajñāpāramitā, but the Dharma-hearer will become diseased. Or vice versa. The Dharma-preacher will wish to go to another region, but the Dharma-hearers will say no to this.
>
> Thus, the Dharma-preacher will be of great desire, while the Dharma-hearer is of few desires—this is not right. In brief, whatever discord there is between Dharma-preacher and Dharma-hearer, all of that is said to be the work of Māra."

---

## Part IV: The Ten Māra-Hooks

In the Āryagaganagañjasūtra it is also stated:⁸

> "Indeed, whatever continuance in unwholesome dharmas there is, and whatever abandonment of wholesome dharmas—all of that is the work of Māra."

In the Āryasāgaramatisūtra it also says:⁹

> "Furthermore, O Blessed One, the bodhisattva who is a forest-dweller, delighting in secluded lodgings, is of few desires, content, secluded, unassociated with householders and renunciants. Because of having few concerns and few tasks, he dwells happily, yet he is not diligent in seeking vast learning, nor does he consider it necessary to cross over to ripen beings, or in the hearing of Dharma, in Dharma-talk, in definitive-meaning discourse.
>
> He is not of the nature of inquiry; he is not devoted to 'What is skillful?' His afflictions do not operate because of his forest-dwelling and because of his single-taste delight. He finds satisfaction merely in the suppression of active defilements. He does not cultivate the path for the eradication of latent tendencies.
>
> Thus he is not practicing for his own benefit or for the benefit of others. This, O Blessed One, is the bodhisattva's **seventh Māra-hook** connected with forest-dwelling...
>
> Furthermore, O Blessed One, the bodhisattva serves, resorts to, and attends upon evil friends who appear to be spiritual friends. They, having diverted him from the means of attraction, having diverted him from the accumulation of merit, from embracing the true Dharma, they engage him in seclusion; they engage him in having few concerns and few tasks. They teach him discourses connected with the Śrāvaka and Pratyekabuddha [vehicles].
>
> And at whatever time the bodhisattva, through dwelling in seclusion, would advance in the Great Vehicle, at that time they engage that bodhisattva in the disturbance of service [to others]. 'Service must certainly be done by a bodhisattva!' And at whatever time the bodhisattva should be engaged in service, at that time they engage him in seclusion.
>
> Thus they say to him: 'Enlightenment is for one of aroused vigor, not for one who is lazy. And if you do not awaken to supreme perfect enlightenment in eight or nine kalpas, you will no longer be capable of awakening to supreme perfect enlightenment.'
>
> There, O Blessed One, it is possible that through excessively aroused vigor the bodhisattva might attain the fruit of nirvāṇa [as an arhat]. This, O Blessed One, is the bodhisattva's **tenth Māra-hook** from those appearing as spiritual friends.
>
> Those who are also Mahāyāna persons, unknowing of the Māra-hooks, who practice dharmas that have been turned away from—with them he finds pleasure. For they become followers of that [path], and the one who resorts to the inferior, not having attained distinction, goes to an inferior destiny—namely, a desert destiny, a destiny of dullness and muteness...up to the **eleventh Māra-hook**."

---

## Part V: The Right Kind of Vigor

Because of this [danger], continuous aroused vigor produces disenchantment with the bodhisattva-state in all ways. Therefore, as stated in the Ratnamegha:¹⁰

> "Here the bodhisattva arouses vigor in all postures. And he arouses it in such a way that he does not generate bodily fatigue, nor mental fatigue. This is called the bodhisattva's continuous vigor.
>
> What kind of vigor is it by which fatigue does not occur? Namely, the undertaking of heavy work by one of little strength, or at an excessive time, or the undertaking of difficult work by one whose aspiration is not yet ripened—such as the giving of one's own flesh, and so forth.
>
> Moreover, one's person has been given. But he [the bodhisattva] prevents it from being consumed at the wrong time. For otherwise, through the bodhisattva's fatigue, through the destruction of the bodhicitta-seed for those very beings, there would be destruction of a great mass of fruit."

Thus in the Gaganagañjasūtra it is also stated:¹¹

> "Expectation of [gifts given] before the proper time is the work of Māra."

---

## Part VI: Protection of One's Person

Nor should the giving up of one's person be left unproduced just because it is not the [proper] time. For without undertaking practice, one would never give.¹² Therefore, having established mindfulness thus, one's person should be protected from:

- Those who contradict the ripening of bodhicitta
- Those who through delusion destroy one's own welfare
- Flesh-eaters [carnivorous beings]¹³
- Those who do karma [harmful agents]

### Kārikā 8 (verse from source)

> *"Just as the seed of the well-appearing medicine tree,*
> *whose root and so forth are to be enjoyed—*
> *even having given it, it should be protected from untimely consumption:*
